‚óŹ Here are my thoughts.

  TT;DR

  M7 is done properly ‚ÄĒ full stop. M8 is done properly too, with one honest 
  caveat: the engine logic is solidly tested, but a clean visual proof of the 
  goose actually riding a dragged window was never captured. No real bugs. The
  code is high quality ‚ÄĒ faithful to both ADRs almost line-for-line, clean
  engine/platform separation, honest capability degradation, and real behavioral
  tests rather than smoke. Codex's M9 plan is strong, but it has the
  asset-policy decision backwards, and I have concrete M9 context to add. I
  ignored the "PRODUCTION-READY ‚úď‚úď‚úď" summary from my own search agent and
  re-verified everything against the source.

  What I checked and found

  I established the contract (plan + ADR 0001/0002), then read the actual
  implementation against it: cursor.rs, foreign_window.rs, task.rs, world.rs,
  the Windows backend lib.rs, and main.rs ‚ÄĒ plus the task board, the M9 plan
  doc, and both changelogs.

  M7 ‚ÄĒ every ADR-0001 clause is honored: platform-free CursorCommand::WarpTo
  queue; nab is pickable only when enabled && warp_supported; seek-at-charge ‚Üí
  bite once ‚Üí capture offset ‚Üí bounded HYPR retarget ‚Üí end on succ_time or
  drop_distance; pat/click suppression proved by a test; warp-failure warns once
  and degrades; --no-mouse-steal present. ~10 real tests.

  M8 ‚ÄĒ every ADR-0002 clause is honored: opaque ForeignWindowId, top-center
  anchor, signed coords; move_window reported as readiness only (engine emits no
  window-move command ‚ÄĒ the correct M8/M9 line); SetWinEventHook callback only
  queues (64-cap), main loop polls GetWindowRect,
  own-overlay/invisible/minimized/non-root all filtered; hook + poll failures
  degrade with a one-time warning; --no-window-ride present. ~11 tests.

  Changelog lockstep: honored ‚ÄĒ matching M7/M8 entries in both CHANGELOG.md and
  HUMAN_CHANGELOG.md.

  Caveats (all low severity)

  1. M8 visual proof gap (the one worth noting) ‚ÄĒ c8a.md admits the ride
  screenshot had a stale Notepad in front, so it "was not a clean visual ride
  proof." Engine behavior is tested; the on-screen ride wasn't cleanly captured,
  which technically misses your own "verify GUI visually" rule. M9 drags
  windows to the beak (inverse machinery), so a clean M9 capture closes this for
  free.
  2. succ_time is 2.5s, not the plan's tentative 1.5s ‚ÄĒ intentional and pinned
  by a test (tied to the hyper burst). Defensible, just an undocumented
  deviation.
  3. .tasks/CLAUDE.md is stale ‚ÄĒ still says "M7 ‚ÄĒ ACTIVE"; the real board has
  M7+M8 Done, M9 Active.
  4. Minor robustness notes for later: nab's seek phase has no timeout (relies
  on the cursor being reachable on the primary monitor ‚ÄĒ matters at M15
  multi-monitor), and start_nab/start_hyper don't guard the single interrupt
  slot the way start_perch_ride does.

  On the M9 plan

  It's genuinely well-structured (command/snapshot boundary, ADR 0003, full
  cross-target matrix, good risk table). I've written 10 code-grounded
  enrichments into my plan file ‚ÄĒ the interrupt-slot precedence trap, the
  suppression hook line, the "window commands aren't .last()-drainable like
  cursor warps" trap, dual Deck+interrupt registration, the z-order answer
  (overlay is already TOPMOST|NOACTIVATE ‚Üí keep collected windows non-topmost),
  the Notepad focus-guard, and folding M8's visual proof into M9 smoke.

  But Codex has the asset policy backwards, and that's the one thing I want to
  confirm before finalizing ‚ÄĒ plus how you want me to hand the enrichments to
  Codex without colliding with its live editing:

     ‚Ēā close it (M9 drags windows to the beak ‚ÄĒ the inverse machinery ‚ÄĒ so a   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā clean M9 capture                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā retroactively validates the M8 ride path too).                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 2. succ_time = 2.5s, not the plan's tentative 1.5s. Intentional and     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pinned by a test                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (mouse_steal_default_drag_time_matches_hyper_burst ties it to           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā HYPER_DURATION). The plan                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā marked MouseSuccTime "TBD, sensible default," so this is a defensible   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā choice, not a bug ‚ÄĒ                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā just an undocumented deviation from a plan constant.                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 3. Stale working-memory cache. .tasks/CLAUDE.md still says "M7 ‚ÄĒ ACTIVE ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (#b7f)" and                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā "M8‚ÄďM19 queued"; the board (TASKS.md) correctly shows M7+M8 Done, M9    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Active. Housekeeping;                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the project-root CLAUDE.md/README.md/AGENTS.md were updated, this       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hot-cache wasn't.                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 4. Minor robustness notes (carry into M9/M15, not blockers):            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā NabState::SeekingMouse has                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā no seek timeout ‚ÄĒ it relies on the cursor being reachable within        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā primary-monitor bounds                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (fine today; add a timeout when multi-monitor M15 lands, since on       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Windows pointer.present                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is hard-coded true). nab/perch are primary-monitor-bound (overlay is    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā primary-only). Ride                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā "pins" by teleporting the goose to the anchor each tick (visually fine  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā during a hand drag).                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā start_nab/start_hyper don't guard on interrupted.is_some() the way      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā start_perch_ride                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā does, so a click mid-hyper can drop the original resume target          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (replaced by a fresh draw) ‚ÄĒ                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā harmless, but see M9 enrichment #1.                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā asset work.                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ---                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Recommended M9 enrichments (code-grounded context for Codex)            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā These come straight from reading the M7/M8 implementation ‚ÄĒ concrete    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā seams M9 should reuse                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā and traps it should avoid:                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 1. Interrupt-slot precedence. World has a single interrupted:           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Option<Box<dyn Task>>                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slot. start_perch_ride guards on interrupted.is_some() (won't stack);   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā start_nab/                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā start_hyper don't (can drop the resume target). M9's collect task is a  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā long-running                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā interrupt and a pickable roaming task ‚ÄĒ it must (a) use the same "don't ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā stack while                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā interrupted" guard, and (b) M9 should define explicit precedence among  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā nab/collect/perch/                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hyper (and document it), rather than inherit today's first-come         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overwrite.                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 2. Suppression hook. Extend World::set_pointer's early-return guard     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (world.rs:172,                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā currently is_cursor_mischief_active() || is_perch_ride_active()) to     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā also cover                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is_collect_window_active(). Add the matching is_*_active() accessor     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā like the existing two.                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 3. Command-drain is NOT .last() for collect. Cursor warp applies only   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the newest command                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (main.rs:125) because intermediate cursor positions are throwaway.      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Window commands are                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā not idempotent ‚ÄĒ Spawn/Close/TypeText/Focus must be drained in full     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā order;                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā only Move may be coalesce-to-latest per target. Do not copy the cursor  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā .last() shortcut.                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 4. Dual registration like nab. nab is both Deck-pickable (world.rs:83,  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā gated by                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mouse_steal.active()) and click/interrupt-triggered. Mirror this:       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā register                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā CollectWindowTask in pickable only when a                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā CollectWindowOptions::active()-style gate                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is true (‚Č•1 kind both available and supported), plus the smoke/force    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā path.                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 5. Anchor + z-order are already solved. Use rig.beak_tip (signed,       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tested ‚ÄĒ it's what nab's                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā offset capture uses, task.rs:221) for windowOffsetToBeak. For the       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā plan's open "z-order"                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā risk: the overlay is WS_EX_TOPMOST | WS_EX_NOACTIVATE (lib.rs:301).     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Keep collected                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā windows non-topmost and the goose stays above them for free; the        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā NOACTIVATE overlay                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā won't fight Notepad for focus.                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 6. Primary-monitor coordinate reality. Overlay = primary monitor only,  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā origin (0,0)                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (main.rs:30); nab/perch clamp to primary_bounds. Spawn/move collected   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā windows within the                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā primary monitor for M9 visual acceptance ‚ÄĒ don't place them at          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā secondary/negative coords                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā expecting the goose to reach them (multi-monitor is M15). Keep the      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā types signed for M15,                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā but the runtime reach is primary-only now.                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 7. Notepad focus/type race (the plan's #1 risk) ‚ÄĒ concrete guard. Match ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the spawned                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Notepad by PID‚ÜíHWND, foreground it, and verify                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā GetForegroundWindow()==that HWND                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā immediately before each SendInput KEYEVENTF_UNICODE burst; abort typing ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā on focus                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mismatch. The overlay being NOACTIVATE helps (it won't steal focus      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā back).                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 8. Fold M8's missing visual proof into M9 smoke. Make a clean           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā goose-over-window capture a                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā first-class M9 acceptance gate; it simultaneously closes the M8 caveat  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā above.                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 9. Constant discipline. New dwell/timeout constants are "TBD sensible   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā defaults" (like                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā MouseSuccTime); pin any intended relationship with a test, as nab did   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā with                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā succ_time == HYPER_DURATION.                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 10. Refresh stale docs in M9.0. Add .tasks/CLAUDE.md (and check         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā .tasks/memory/projects/ honk300.md) to the M9.0 doc-reconciliation list ‚Ēā

     /plan to edit
     Verify M7/M8 + enrich M9 ‚ÄĒ audit & advisory

     Context

     Codex implemented M7 (cursor mischief) and M8 (foreign-window
     watch-and-ride) and is
     right now planning M9 (collect-window dispatcher). Emmett asked me to (1)
     verify M7/M8
     were done properly, (2) review the updated M9 plan, and (3) add detail to
     M9 from my
     analysis so Codex has full context. This is a claim-testing / 
     Scientific-Inquiry task:
     the claim under test is "Codex completed M7 and M8 properly." I treated the
     prior
     "COMPLETE & PRODUCTION-READY" agent summary as an unverified assertion and
     re-derived the
     verdict by reading the actual source against the ADR contracts
     (falsification, not
     confirmation). The task board server was already running; I did not start
     it ‚ÄĒ I read
     its backing file .tasks/TASKS.md.

     Method: extracted the acceptance contract from honk300_plan.md + ADR 0001
     (M7) + ADR 0002
     (M8), then checked it line-by-line against
     crates/honk-engine/src/{cursor,foreign_window, task,world}.rs,
     crates/honk-platform-windows/src/lib.rs, and src/main.rs; cross-checked
     the claimed status in .tasks/ and the lockstep changelogs.

     ---
     Verdict

     M7 ‚ÄĒ PASS (faithful & complete). M8 ‚ÄĒ PASS on contract/engine; ONE real 
     caveat: the
     end-to-end visual ride was never cleanly captured. No hard bugs found. The
     work is
     genuinely high quality: clean engine/platform separation, honest capability
     degradation,
     and real behavioral tests (not smoke).

     M7 cursor mischief ‚ÄĒ every ADR-0001 clause honored

     - Engine stays platform-free: CursorCommand::WarpTo(Vec2) queue drained by
     the backend; no
     OS calls in honk-engine. (cursor.rs, task.rs:232, world.rs:122)
     - Capability gating: MouseStealOptions::active() = enabled && 
     warp_supported; NabMouseTask
     is pickable only when active (world.rs:83); click‚Üínab when supported, else
     click‚Üíhyper
     fallback (world.rs:194, tick precedence world.rs:249-263).
     - Nab lifecycle matches the ADR exactly: seek at charge speed ‚Üí bite once
     (bite_played)
     ‚Üí capture beak-to-cursor offset ‚Üí bounded HYPR-style retarget (not a
     straight line) ‚Üí
     end on succ_time or drop_distance pull-away. (task.rs:200-268)
     - Suppression: set_pointer early-returns during nab so synthetic motion
     can't pat or stack
     hyper ‚ÄĒ proved by test nab_suppresses_pat_and_click_hyper_interactions.
     (world.rs:172)
     - Backend: warp_cursor = thin SetCursorPos; runtime failure ‚Üí
     set_cursor_warp_supported( false) + warn once + continue (main.rs:125-133);
     --no-mouse-steal present.
     - 10 dedicated engine/world tests covering disabled/unsupported,
     seek/grab/drag/drop/timeout,
     retarget, command-drain-once.

     M8 foreign-window perch & ride ‚ÄĒ every ADR-0002 clause honored

     - Opaque ForeignWindowId(u64); ForeignWindowSnapshot{id,rect,ride_anchor}
     fed only while a
     drag is active; top-center anchor; signed coords (negative-monitor test
     present).
     - move_window reported as readiness data only ‚ÄĒ engine emits no window-move
     command
     (correct M8/M9 boundary; there is no window-command queue yet).
     (foreign_window.rs:41)
     - PerchRideTask = transient interrupt reusing the resume path; seek at run
     speed ‚Üí pin to
     moving anchor until release; abandons cleanly on release-before-arrival or
     capability
     loss. (task.rs:300-346, world.rs:265-271)
     - Backend: SetWinEventHook(MOVESIZESTART..MOVESIZEEND, 
     OUTOFCONTEXT|SKIPOWNPROCESS); callback
     only queues events (64-cap bounded); main loop polls GetWindowRect;
     is_foreign_top_ level_window filters
     own-overlay/invisible/minimized/non-root/invalid. (lib.rs:87-204)
     - Hook-setup failure and geometry-poll failure both degrade with a one-time
     warning and
     set_foreign_window_watch_supported(false) (main.rs:36-47, 96-116);
     --no-window-ride
     present.
     - 9 dedicated tests + 2 Windows helper tests.

     Discrepancies / caveats (all low severity)

     1. M8 visual acceptance gap (the one that matters). The engine behavior is
     fully tested
     headlessly and the watcher runs without error, but a clean screenshot/video
     of the goose
     running to and riding a dragged window was never captured ‚ÄĒ c8a.md admits
     the capture had
     a stale Notepad in front, so it "was not a clean visual ride proof." The
     repo's own rule
     (.tasks/CLAUDE.md ‚Üí "Verify GUI visually before claiming it works") was
     therefore not
     fully met for M8. Not a code defect ‚ÄĒ an unmet verification standard. M9's
     smoke can
     close it (M9 drags windows to the beak ‚ÄĒ the inverse machinery ‚ÄĒ so a clean
     M9 capture
     retroactively validates the M8 ride path too).
     2. succ_time = 2.5s, not the plan's tentative 1.5s. Intentional and pinned 
     by a test
     (mouse_steal_default_drag_time_matches_hyper_burst ties it to
     HYPER_DURATION). The plan
     marked MouseSuccTime "TBD, sensible default," so this is a defensible
     choice, not a bug ‚ÄĒ
     just an undocumented deviation from a plan constant.
     3. Stale working-memory cache. .tasks/CLAUDE.md still says "M7 ‚ÄĒ ACTIVE
     (#b7f)" and
     "M8‚ÄďM19 queued"; the board (TASKS.md) correctly shows M7+M8 Done, M9
     Active. Housekeeping;
     the project-root CLAUDE.md/README.md/AGENTS.md were updated, this hot-cache
     wasn't.
     4. Minor robustness notes (carry into M9/M15, not blockers):
     NabState::SeekingMouse has
     no seek timeout ‚ÄĒ it relies on the cursor being reachable within
     primary-monitor bounds
     (fine today; add a timeout when multi-monitor M15 lands, since on Windows
     pointer.present
     is hard-coded true). nab/perch are primary-monitor-bound (overlay is
     primary-only). Ride
     "pins" by teleporting the goose to the anchor each tick (visually fine
     during a hand drag).
     start_nab/start_hyper don't guard on interrupted.is_some() the way
     start_perch_ride
     does, so a click mid-hyper can drop the original resume target (replaced by
     a fresh draw) ‚ÄĒ
     harmless, but see M9 enrichment #1.

     Review of the updated M9 plan

     The M9 plan (docs/thinking/2026-06-27-m9-collect-window-plan.md + board
     card #e9b +
     e9b.md) is strong ‚ÄĒ genuinely the right shape. It correctly: keeps the
     command/snapshot
     boundary in honk-engine; plans ADR 0003; sequences M9.0‚ÜíM9.7; carries the
     full cross-target
     matrix; gates on capabilities not compile targets; and caught the 
     asset-policy conflict
     (see below). The issue-tree, risk table, and acceptance checklist are
     thorough. Confidence in
     its architecture: high.

     The one thing it gets backwards ‚ÄĒ the asset-policy default (see decision 
     below). Codex
     defaulted M9 to no-copy / author-fresh, treating CLAUDE.md as the stale
     source. But the
     project-root CLAUDE.md (authoritative, marked as overriding) explicitly
     says the
     "regenerate memes / author fresh notes" plan is superseded ‚ÄĒ copy the 
     originals 1:1 (the
     policy was updated at M5, commit a33dcbc). It's honk300_plan.md + AGENTS.md
     that are
     stale, not CLAUDE.md. So the reconciliation should very likely go the
     opposite way from
     Codex's default. This must be settled before M9.1 ‚ÄĒ it inverts the asset

     ---
     Recommended M9 enrichments (code-grounded context for Codex)

     These come straight from reading the M7/M8 implementation ‚ÄĒ concrete seams
     M9 should reuse
     and traps it should avoid:

     1. Interrupt-slot precedence. World has a single interrupted: 
     Option<Box<dyn Task>>
     slot. start_perch_ride guards on interrupted.is_some() (won't stack);
     start_nab/
     start_hyper don't (can drop the resume target). M9's collect task is a
     long-running
     interrupt and a pickable roaming task ‚ÄĒ it must (a) use the same "don't
     stack while
     interrupted" guard, and (b) M9 should define explicit precedence among
     nab/collect/perch/
     hyper (and document it), rather than inherit today's first-come overwrite.
     2. Suppression hook. Extend World::set_pointer's early-return guard
     (world.rs:172,
     currently is_cursor_mischief_active() || is_perch_ride_active()) to also
     cover
     is_collect_window_active(). Add the matching is_*_active() accessor like
     the existing two.
     3. Command-drain is NOT .last() for collect. Cursor warp applies only the
     newest command
     (main.rs:125) because intermediate cursor positions are throwaway. Window 
     commands are
     not idempotent ‚ÄĒ Spawn/Close/TypeText/Focus must be drained in full order;
     only Move may be coalesce-to-latest per target. Do not copy the cursor
     .last() shortcut.
     4. Dual registration like nab. nab is both Deck-pickable (world.rs:83,
     gated by
     mouse_steal.active()) and click/interrupt-triggered. Mirror this: register
     CollectWindowTask in pickable only when a
     CollectWindowOptions::active()-style gate
     is true (‚Č•1 kind both available and supported), plus the smoke/force path.
     5. Anchor + z-order are already solved. Use rig.beak_tip (signed, tested ‚ÄĒ
     it's what nab's
     offset capture uses, task.rs:221) for windowOffsetToBeak. For the plan's
     open "z-order"
     risk: the overlay is WS_EX_TOPMOST | WS_EX_NOACTIVATE (lib.rs:301). Keep 
     collected
     windows non-topmost and the goose stays above them for free; the NOACTIVATE
     overlay
     won't fight Notepad for focus.
     6. Primary-monitor coordinate reality. Overlay = primary monitor only,
     origin (0,0)
     (main.rs:30); nab/perch clamp to primary_bounds. Spawn/move collected
     windows within the
     primary monitor for M9 visual acceptance ‚ÄĒ don't place them at
     secondary/negative coords
     expecting the goose to reach them (multi-monitor is M15). Keep the types
     signed for M15,
     but the runtime reach is primary-only now.
     7. Notepad focus/type race (the plan's #1 risk) ‚ÄĒ concrete guard. Match the
     spawned
     Notepad by PID‚ÜíHWND, foreground it, and verify GetForegroundWindow()==that 
     HWND
     immediately before each SendInput KEYEVENTF_UNICODE burst; abort typing on
     focus
     mismatch. The overlay being NOACTIVATE helps (it won't steal focus back).
     8. Fold M8's missing visual proof into M9 smoke. Make a clean
     goose-over-window capture a
     first-class M9 acceptance gate; it simultaneously closes the M8 caveat
     above.
     9. Constant discipline. New dwell/timeout constants are "TBD sensible
     defaults" (like
     MouseSuccTime); pin any intended relationship with a test, as nab did with
     succ_time == HYPER_DURATION.
     10. Refresh stale docs in M9.0. Add .tasks/CLAUDE.md (and check
     .tasks/memory/projects/ honk300.md) to the M9.0 doc-reconciliation list ‚ÄĒ
     its Status still reads "M7 ACTIVE."

      514 +## M9 enrichments (code-grounded ‚ÄĒ concrete seams to reuse, tr
          +aps to avoid)                                                 
      515 +                                                              
      516 +1. **Interrupt-slot precedence.** `World` has a single `interr
          +upted: Option<Box<dyn Task>>`                                 
      517 +   slot. `start_perch_ride` guards on `interrupted.is_some()` 
          +(won't stack); `start_nab`/                                   
      518 +   `start_hyper` do **not** (can drop the resume target). `Col
          +lectWindowTask` is a long-running                             
      519 +   interrupt *and* a pickable roaming task ‚ÄĒ it must (a) use t
          +he same "don't stack while                                    
      520 +   interrupted" guard, and (b) define + document explicit prec
          +edence among                                                  
      521 +   nab/collect/perch/hyper rather than inherit today's first-c
          +ome overwrite.                                                
      522 +2. **Suppression hook.** Extend `World::set_pointer`'s early-r
          +eturn guard (`world.rs:172`,                                  
      523 +   currently `is_cursor_mischief_active() || is_perch_ride_act
          +ive()`) to also cover                                         
      524 +   `is_collect_window_active()`; add the matching `is_*_active
          +()` accessor.                                                 
      525 +3. **Command-drain is NOT `.last()` for collect.** Cursor warp
          + applies only the newest command                              
      526 +   (`main.rs:125`) because intermediate cursor positions are t
          +hrowaway. **Window commands are                               
      527 +   not idempotent** ‚ÄĒ `Spawn`/`Close`/`TypeText`/`Focus` must 
          +be drained **in full order**;                                 
      528 +   only `Move` may coalesce-to-latest per target. Do not copy 
          +the cursor `.last()` shortcut.                                
      529 +4. **Dual registration like nab.** nab is both Deck-pickable (
          +`world.rs:83`, gated by                                       
      530 +   `mouse_steal.active()`) and click/interrupt-triggered. Mirr
          +or it: register                                               
      531 +   `CollectWindowTask` in `pickable` **only when** a `CollectW
          +indowOptions::active()`-style gate                            
      532 +   is true (‚Č•1 kind both available *and* supported), plus the 
          +smoke/force path.                                             
      533 +5. **Anchor + z-order are already solved.** Use `rig.beak_tip`
          + (signed, tested ‚ÄĒ it's what nab's                            
      534 +   offset capture uses at `task.rs:221`) for `windowOffsetToBe
          +ak`. For the "z-order" risk: the                              
      535 +   overlay is `WS_EX_TOPMOST | WS_EX_NOACTIVATE` (`lib.rs:301`
          +), so **keep collected windows                                
      536 +   non-topmost** and the goose stays above them for free; the 
          +`NOACTIVATE` overlay won't fight                              
      537 +   Notepad for focus.                                         
      538 +6. **Primary-monitor coordinate reality.** Overlay = primary m
          +onitor only, origin (0,0)                                     
      539 +   (`main.rs:30`); nab/perch clamp to `primary_bounds`. Spawn/
          +move collected windows within the                             
      540 +   primary monitor for M9 visual acceptance ‚ÄĒ don't place them
          + at secondary/negative coords                                 
      541 +   expecting the goose to reach them (multi-monitor is M15). K
          +eep *types* signed for M15; the                               
      542 +   *runtime* reach is primary-only now.                       
      543 +7. **Notepad focus/type race (the #1 risk) ‚ÄĒ concrete guard.**
          + Match the spawned Notepad by                                 
      544 +   PID‚ÜíHWND, foreground it, and verify `GetForegroundWindow() 
          +== that HWND` immediately before                              
      545 +   each `SendInput` `KEYEVENTF_UNICODE` burst; abort typing on
          + focus mismatch. The overlay being                            
      546 +   `NOACTIVATE` helps (it won't steal focus back).            
      547 +8. **Fold M8's missing visual proof into M9 smoke.** Make a cl
          +ean goose-over-window capture a                               
      548 +   first-class M9 acceptance gate; it simultaneously closes th
          +e M8 caveat above.                                            
      549 +9. **Constant discipline.** New dwell/timeout constants are "T
          +BD sensible defaults" (like                                   
      550 +   `MouseSuccTime`); pin any intended relationship with a test
          +, as nab did with                                             
      551 +   `succ_time == HYPER_DURATION`.                             
      552 +10. **Refresh stale docs in M9.0.** Add `.tasks/CLAUDE.md` (an
          +d check                                                       
      553 +    `.tasks/memory/projects/honk300.md`) to the M9.0 doc-recon
          +ciliation list ‚ÄĒ its Status still                             
      554 +    reads "M7 ACTIVE."

‚óŹ The current (M12) reload path is actually solid where it matters most: on
  Reload it calls Config::load_existing(&options.config_path) ‚ÄĒ genuinely
  re-reading the TOML from disk, rebuilding effective, and applying via
  world.apply_options(...); on a parse error it keeps the prior config with a
  warning (validate-then-apply, atomic). So the M10-style "no-op reload" concern
  was fixed. But I notice something suspect: cursor_warp_supported is computed
  once at startup (line 31-32) from config.safety.no_mouse_steal and never 
  recomputed on reload (line 106 passes the fixed value) ‚ÄĒ that smells like an
  asymmetric hot-apply bug. Let me read effective_options to confirm:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Confirmed a second real bug independently. At startup cursor_warp_supported
  (line 31-32) is set from !(cli no_mouse_steal || config.safety.no_mouse_steal)
  ‚ÄĒ this conflates the user's preference with the backend capability, then
  feeds it into BackendState.cursor_warp_supported. It's only ever flipped to
  false (on warp failure, line 242) and is never recomputed on reload. So if you
  start with mouse-steal off (or it fails once), then re-enable it in config
  and reload, it stays permanently off ‚ÄĒ an asymmetric hot-apply failure that 
  also violates M12.1's "user-enabled vs backend-supported must stay 
  distinguishable" rule. That's almost certainly the M12 agent's second MAJOR.

  While the agents finish fetching their full reports, let me verify the

  #: 1

  Finding: Disabling the pat/hearts toggle silently kills click‚Üíhyper (M6) and 
    click‚Üínab (M7). clicked is derived from hovering, which is gated by
    interaction.pat_streak. Its test only checks the pat side, so the click
    regression is unguarded. (I verified this in code.)
  Evidence: world.rs:327-342
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  #: 2
  Sev: MAJOR
  Finding: Mouse-steal can't be re-enabled via reload. cursor_warp_supported (a
    backend capability) is seeded from the user preference no_mouse_steal at
    startup, only ever flipped false, never recomputed on reload. Start off ‚Üí
    enable in config ‚Üí reload = stays dead till restart. Violates the
    "user-enabled vs backend-supported stay distinguishable" rule. (I  verified 
    this in code.)
  Evidence: runtime/windows.rs:31-32, 106, 240-248
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ

    spawn/move failure degrades via set_collect_window_supported(false), but
  that

  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ

  Process / plan divergences (my own):
  - No ADR 0005/0006. M7‚Üí0001, M8‚Üí0002, M9‚Üí0003, M10‚Üí0004 ‚ÄĒ but M11/M12 added
  none, despite the engine WorldOptions contract growing
  (InteractionOptions/TimingOptions) and milestone-scope changes. That's
  contrary to CLAUDE.md's ADR discipline.
  - tokio::select! loop (plan ¬ß9) was replaced by a synchronous
  event::poll(100ms) loop. Works, but diverges from the stated stack (and pulls
  tokio into Cargo.lock for little benefit).
  - Three-name CLI is deferred to M19 by design ‚ÄĒ only one [[bin]] (honk300)
  exists; goose/honk are packaging symlinks later. So M11's literal acceptance
  examples (goose plz, honk bad) aren't runnable yet ‚ÄĒ the grammar works
  name-agnostically (honk300 plz/honk300 bad). "goose-speak" is correctly
  implemented as a finite phrase‚Üísubcommand map, not per-name output (which the
  plan doesn't require).

  What's genuinely solid

  Engine purity is preserved ‚ÄĒ honk-engine is still #![forbid(unsafe_code)], no
  OS deps, and the config plumbing leaks no paths/handles into it. The
  control-plane extraction to honk-control is a verified pure rename (IPC
  protocol byte-identical to M10). TOML is atomic (temp-file + persist),
  versioned (goose_config_version), forward-tolerant, with validation. The TUI
  is a real Action ‚Üí apply() reducer with correct panic-safe terminal restore,
  and Poke-over-IPC works. Reload does a real on-disk re-read (not the M10-style
  no-op).

       5 +use std::sync::mpsc::{self, Receiver, Sender};                 
       6 +use std::time::Duration;                                       
       7  
       8 +/// How long the transport waits for the sim to answer a comman
         +d before giving up.                                            
       9 +const RESPONSE_TIMEOUT: Duration = Duration::from_secs(2);     
      10 +                                                               
      11  #[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
      12  pub enum SingletonStatus {
      13      Acquired,
      14      AlreadyRunning,
      15  }
      16  
      17 +/// A decoded command paired with a one-shot channel back to th
         +e waiting transport.                                           
      18 +///                                                            
      19 +/// The server thread hands this to the sim and blocks (briefly
         +) on the response, so a caller                                 
      20 +/// of `do <action>` or `reload` learns the real outcome instea
         +d of a blanket "received".                                     
      21 +pub struct ControlRequest {                                    
      22 +    command: ControlCommand,                                   
      23 +    responder: Sender<ControlResponse>,                        
      24 +}                                                              
      25 +                                                               
      26 +impl ControlRequest {                                          
      27 +    pub(crate) fn new(command: ControlCommand, responder: Sende
         +r<ControlResponse>) -> Self {                                  
      28 +        Self { command, responder }                            
      29 +    }                                                          
      30 +                                                               
      31 +    /// The requested command.                                 
      32 +    pub fn command(&self) -> ControlCommand {                  
      33 +        self.command                                           
      34 +    }                                                          
      35 +                                                               
      36 +    /// Answer the waiting transport with this command's outcom
         +e. Consumes the request so each                                
      37 +    /// command is answered once; if the transport already time
         +d out, the send is dropped.                                    
      38 +    pub fn respond(self, response: ControlResponse) {          
      39 +        let _ = self.responder.send(response);                 
      40 +    }                                                          
      41 +}                                                              
      42 +                                                               
      43 +/// Hand a decoded command to the sim and block until it answer
         +s (or the wait times out).                                     
      44 +fn dispatch(tx: &Sender<ControlRequest>, command: ControlComman
         +d) -> ControlResponse {                                        
      45 +    let (resp_tx, resp_rx) = mpsc::channel();                  
      46 +    if tx.send(ControlRequest::new(command, resp_tx)).is_err() 
         +{                                                              
      47 +        return ControlResponse::Err("SERVER_CLOSED".into());   
      48 +    }                                                          
      49 +    resp_rx                                                    
      50 +        .recv_timeout(RESPONSE_TIMEOUT)                        
      51 +        .unwrap_or_else(|_| ControlResponse::Err("TIMEOUT".into
         +()))                                                           
      52 +}                                                              
      53 +                                                               
      54  pub struct Singleton {
      55      _imp: imp::Singleton,
      56  }

      258    canonical and summarizing the decided direction (three-name 
           goose-speak CLI, ratatui config
      259    TUI, new autonomous behaviors, no external mods / no tray, a
           ll-OS/all-arch builds).
      260  
      261 +### Fixed                                                     
      262 +- **Control responses now report the real outcome (M11 round-t
          +rip).** `honk300 do <action>` and                             
      263 +  `reload` previously always answered `OK` because the server 
          +thread responded at command-enqueue                           
      264 +  time, before the simulation ran. The transport now completes
          + a request/response round-trip:                               
      265 +  `honk-control` gained `ControlRequest`, a bounded (2 s) wait
          + for the sim's answer, and a                                  
      266 +  `PokeOutcome`‚Üí`ControlResponse` mapping (`Busy` ‚Üí `ERR BUSY`
          +, `Unsupported` ‚Üí `ERR UNSUPPORTED`,                          
      267 +  reload failure ‚Üí `ERR RELOAD_REJECTED`, timeout ‚Üí `ERR TIMEO
          +UT`). The CLI/TUI "rejected: {code}"                          
      268 +  paths now actually fire. (ADR 0005.)                        
      269 +- **Cursor-warp capability is no longer seeded from the mouse-
          +steal preference (M12 reload).** The                          
      270 +  Windows runtime initialized `cursor_warp_supported` from `!n
          +o_mouse_steal`, latching warp off so                          
      271 +  a config edit that re-enabled mouse steal never took effect 
          +until restart. It is now a pure                               
      272 +  platform capability (`true` on Windows, via `initial_cursor_
          +warp_supported`) that degrades only                           
      273 +  on a real warp failure; the preference is applied solely thr
          +ough `MouseStealOptions::enabled`.                            
      274 +  (ADR 0006.)                                                 
      275 +- **Collect-window capability loss now survives reload (M12).*
          +* A backend collect-window failure                            
      276 +  was recorded only in engine state and was overwritten by the
          + next reload, so the goose kept                               
      277 +  retrying a dead capability. `BackendState` gained `collect_w
          +indow_supported`, threaded through                            
      278 +  `Config::effective_options`, so the loss is durable across r
          +eloads. (ADR 0006.)                                           
      279 +- **Disabling the pat streak no longer disables clicking (M12 
          +interaction).** `interaction.pat_streak`                      
      280 +  gated the click reaction as well as pats. It now scopes to t
          +he hover-pat hearts/calm only;                                
      281 +  clicking the goose still triggers a hyper burst (or a cursor
          + nab when mouse steal is supported).                          
      282 +  (ADR 0006.)                                                 
      283 +

           or vector effects or
